## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: materials science / constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, a fundamental problem in constitutive modeling where stress depends on mechanical strain and temperature through elastic, plastic, and/or thermal softening mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (exponential): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (thermally activated modulus decay)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear plastic hardening)
- Hollomon equation with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (power-law hardening with Arrhenius-type thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook thermal softening (power form): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - T)**c3 (power-law thermal softening relative to melting point)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse form: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic + plastic contributions)
- Voce-type saturation hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Voce with temperature: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * exp(c2 * T) (saturation hardening with thermal softening)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (polynomial constitutive law)
- Arrhenius-type flow stress: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * (c2 * T)) * sinh(c3 * epsilon) (hyperbolic sine creep law)
- Neo-Hookean type: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * epsilon**3) * (c2 + c3 * T) (hyperelastic with temperature dependence)
- Ludwik equation with temperature: sigma = c0 * (c1 + epsilon)**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (generalized hardening with thermal effects)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → multiplicative factor (c0 + c1*T) or exp(c2*T) modifying the stress-strain relationship
- Strain hardening in plasticity → power-law epsilon**c with exponent typically 0 < c < 1 for metals
- Stress saturation at large strains → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) form indicating dislocation saturation
- Melting-point referenced softening → (c0 - T)**c1 where c0 represents a reference/melting temperature
- Elastic-plastic transition → sum of linear term (c0*epsilon) and nonlinear term (c1*epsilon**c2) representing dual regimes
- Thermally activated deformation → Arrhenius factor exp(c0*T) reflecting activation energy for dislocation motion
- Strain-temperature coupling → product form f(epsilon)*g(T) indicating separable mechanical and thermal contributions
- Hyperbolic sine flow rule → sinh(c*epsilon) appearing in high-temperature creep and hot deformation models
